## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables map directly to a thermo-mechanical constitutive law where stress sigma depends on strain epsilon via elastic/plastic hardening and depends on temperature T via temperature-dependent modulus, yield/flow stress, and thermal expansion/softening. Common models combine a strain response (linear, power-law, saturating) with multiplicative or additive temperature dependence.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke law: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear thermoelasticity with E(T))
- Exponential-softened elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * T) (modulus decreases rapidly with temperature)
- Constrained thermal strain (thermoelastic shift): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (thermal expansion causes stress offset under constraint)
- Quadratic/nonlinear elastic expansion with T-coupling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (moderate-strain nonlinearity and temperature-dependent tangent modulus)
- Hollomon power-law hardening with thermal prefactor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (plastic work hardening with temperature-dependent strength)
- Temperature-dependent hardening exponent: sigma = c0 * epsilon**(c1 + c2 * T) (hardening rate changes with temperature)
- Ludwik-type (offset + power-law) with T-dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**c4 (yield/offset stress plus hardening)
- Voce saturation hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon)) (approach to saturation stress; temperature shifts both yield and saturation)
- Double-stage hardening (sum of saturations): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) + c3 * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon)) + c5 * T (captures two mechanisms with different strain scales)
- Logarithmic hardening with temperature scaling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * log(1 + c3 * epsilon) (empirical work hardening with diminishing slope)
- Hyperelastic stretch-power form with T-dependent stiffness: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * ((1 + epsilon)**c2 - (1 + epsilon)**(-c3)) (nonlinear elastic response in terms of stretch 1+epsilon)
- Thermal-softening of a strain polynomial: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * exp(-c3 * T) (general stress-strain curve scaled down by temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent modulus/yield commonly appears as a prefactor multiplying the entire strain-response term: sigma = g(T) * f(epsilon).
- Thermal expansion under constraint is modeled by shifting strain: epsilon_eff = epsilon - c * (T - T0), so sigma depends on epsilon and T through epsilon_eff.
- Work-hardening often follows concave-down growth in epsilon; saturation behavior is captured by 1 - exp(-c * epsilon) rather than unbounded polynomials.
- Hardening that slows with strain can be represented by log(1 + c * epsilon) terms, giving high initial slope and diminishing increments.
- If temperature mainly reduces strength uniformly, an exponential or power softening factor g(T) (e.g., exp(-c*T) or (c0 - c1*T)**c2 where valid) is typical.
- When temperature changes the shape of the stress-strain curve (not just scale), allow exponents or saturation rates to depend on T: epsilon**(c0 + c1*T) or exp(-(c0 + c1*T)*epsilon).
- For large deformations, replacing epsilon with stretch (1 + epsilon) and using power differences can better represent nonlinear elasticity and asymmetry in tension/compression.
- Additive decomposition sigma = sigma0(T) + sigma_hard(epsilon, T) is common when separating a temperature-dependent yield/offset stress from subsequent hardening.
